10029{_}1973{_}Henshaw had been caught and fascinated by Edith Morriston's beauty, and being, as was obvious, a man of energy and determination, was now in some subtle way making use of the tragedy as a means of forcing his unwelcome attentions on her.
10029{_}1974{_}How otherwise could this astounding familiarity be arrived at?
10029{_}1975{_}Sick with disgust and indignation, Gifford turned away and retraced his steps through the wood, dismissing, as likely to lead to a false position, his first impulse to appear on the scene and stop, at any rate for that day, Henshaw's designs.
10029{_}1976{_}He felt that to act precipitately might do less good than harm.
10029{_}1977{_}He was, after all, on private ground there, and had no right to intrude upon what in all likelihood Miss Morriston wished to be a secluded interview.
10029{_}1978{_}What course he would take in the future was another matter, and one which demanded instant and serious consideration.
10029{_}1979{_}The right line to adopt was indeed a perplexing problem.
10029{_}1980{_}Gifford recalled Morriston's story of having met Henshaw hanging about more or less mysteriously in the plantation, and the annoyance he had expressed at the encounter.
10029{_}1981{_}The reason was plain enough now.
10029{_}1982{_}Of course the man was waiting either to waylay Edith Morriston or to meet her by appointment.
10029{_}1983{_}It was not a pleasant reflection; since the fact showed that these clandestine meetings had probably been going on for some days past.
10029{_}1984{_}That Henshaw's object was more or less disreputable could not be doubted, and to Gifford the amazing and troubling part of it was that Edith Morriston, the very last woman he would have suspected of consenting to such a course, who had professed an absolute dislike and repugnance to Henshaw, and fear of his annoying presence, should be meeting him thus willingly.
10029{_}1985{_}Had he not seen them with his own eyes he would have scoffed at the idea as something inconceivable.
10029{_}1986{_}Now what was he to do?
10029{_}1987{_}For it was clear that, justified or not as he might be thought in interfering in matters which did not concern him, something must be done.
10029{_}1988{_}The one obvious course which it seemed he ought to take was to give Richard Morriston a hint of what was on foot, if not a stronger and more explicit statement.
10029{_}1989{_}For that Morriston could be privy to the correspondence between his sister and Henshaw was quite unlikely.
10029{_}1990{_}If anything underhand was going on, if Henshaw was holding some threat over the girl or pursuing her with unwelcome attentions her brother, as her natural guardian, should be warned.
10029{_}1991{_}That seemed to Gifford his manifest duty.
10029{_}1992{_}And yet he shrank from anything which might seem treachery towards the girl.
10029{_}1993{_}For, if she needed her brother's help and protection against the man, it would be an easy matter for her to complain of his persecution.
10029{_}1994{_}Why, he wondered, had she not done so?
10029{_}1995{_}It was all very mysterious.
10029{_}1996{_}He tried to imagine how the position had come about.
10029{_}1997{_}On Henshaw's side it was plain enough.
10029{_}1998{_}Miss Morriston was not only a strikingly handsome girl, but she was an heiress, possessing, according to Kelson, a considerable fortune in her own right.
10029{_}1999{_}There, clearly, was Henshaw's motive; an incentive to an unscrupulous man to use every art, fair and unfair, to force himself into her favour.
10029{_}2000{_}But how had he succeeded so quickly as to make this rather haughty, reserved girl consent to meet in secret the man whom she professed to dislike and avoid?
10029{_}2001{_}That this unpleasantly sharp, pushing product of the less dignified side of the law could have any personal attraction for one of Edith Morriston's taste and discrimination was impossible.
10029{_}2002{_}And yet there the challenging fact remained that confidential relations had been established between the disparate pair.
10029{_}2003{_}Was it possible that this man could have found out something connecting Edith Morriston with his brother's death?
10029{_}2004{_}The feasibility of the idea came as a shock to Gifford.
10029{_}2005{_}He stopped dead in his walk as the notion took form in his brain.
10029{_}2006{_}The possibilities of this most mysterious case were too complicated to be grasped at once.
10029{_}2007{_}And so with his mind in a whirl of vague conjecture and apprehension he reached his hotel.
10029{_}2008{_}And there a new development in the mystery awaited him.
10029{_}2009{_}CHAPTER XV  ANOTHER DISCOVERY   Kelson was in their sitting-room reading the _Field_.
10029{_}2010{_}He started up as Gifford entered, and flung away the paper.
10029{_}2011{_}"My dear Hugh, I've been waiting for you," he exclaimed.
10029{_}2012{_}"What's the matter?
10029{_}2013{_}Anything wrong?"
10029{_}2014{_}Gifford asked with a certain apprehensive curiosity, as he noticed signs of suppressed excitement in his friend's face.
10029{_}2015{_}"I don't know whether it's all wrong or whether it is all right," Kelson replied.
10029{_}2016{_}"Anyhow it has relieved my mind a good deal."
10029{_}2017{_}Controlling his own tendency to excitement, Gifford put aside his hat and stick and sat down.
10029{_}2018{_}"Let's hear it," he said quietly.
10029{_}2019{_}"Well, another unaccountable thing has, it appears, happened at Wynford Place.
10029{_}2020{_}A pendant, or whatever you call it, to that which has been troubling Muriel.
10029{_}2021{_}What do you think?
10029{_}2022{_}As I was riding along the Loxford road this afternoon I met Dick Morriston, and he told me that another discovery of blood-stains has been made at Wynford.
10029{_}2023{_}On a girl's ball-dress too.
10029{_}2024{_}And on whose do you suppose it is?"
10029{_}2025{_}"Not Miss Morriston's?"
10029{_}2026{_}Gifford suggested breathlessly.
10029{_}2027{_}Kelson nodded, with a slight look of surprise at the correctness of the guess.
10029{_}2028{_}"Yes.
10029{_}2029{_}Isn't it queer?
10029{_}2030{_}Poor old Dick is in rather a way about it, and I must say the whole business is decidedly mysterious."
10029{_}2031{_}Gifford was thinking keenly.
10029{_}2032{_}"How did it come out?
10029{_}2033{_}Who found the marks?"
10029{_}2034{_}he asked.
10029{_}2035{_}"Well," Kelson answered, "it appears that Edith Morriston's maid found them some days ago, in fact the day after a similar discovery had been made on Muriel's gown.
10029{_}2036{_}She had brought the dress which her mistress had worn at the Hunt Ball out of the wardrobe where it hung, in order to fold it away.
10029{_}2037{_}She appears to have spread it on the bed where the sun shone on it and in the strong light she noticed on the dark material some brownish discolorations.
10029{_}2038{_}With what had happened about the other dress in her mind, she examined the marks closely, and with such intentness as to raise the curiosity of a housemaid who happened to come into the room.
10029{_}2039{_}At first Miss Morriston's maid tried to put her off, but the other girl, who was sharp-eyed, had seen the marks, was not to be hood-winked, and the mischief was done.
10029{_}2040{_}The housemaid seems to be a foolish, babbling creature, and the discovery soon became the talk of the servants' hall, whence it spread till it reached the police."
10029{_}2041{_}"And what are they doing about it?"
10029{_}2042{_}Gifford asked.
10029{_}2043{_}"Morriston says they've had a detective up at the house examining the gown; being so utterly at sea over the affair the police are doubtless glad to catch at anything.
10029{_}2044{_}There seems little question that the stains are blood, and that makes the whole business still more puzzling.
10029{_}2045{_}Dick Morriston is naturally very exercised about it, but I am very glad for Muriel's sake that the second discovery has been made.
10029{_}2046{_}In fact I have been just waiting till I saw you before riding over to tell her of it, and relieve her mind."
10029{_}2047{_}"Yes," Gifford responded mechanically, "of course it removes any serious suspicion from Miss Tredworth."
10029{_}2048{_}"And," said Kelson eagerly, "it divides the odium, if there is any.
10029{_}2049{_}In fact, to my mind, it reduces the whole suspicion to an absurdity.
10029{_}2050{_}For that both girls could have been concerned in Henshaw's death is absolutely incredible."
10029{_}2051{_}"Yes," Gifford agreed thoughtfully; "they could not both have had a hand in it."
10029{_}2052{_}"Or either, for that matter," Kelson returned with a laugh.
10029{_}2053{_}"Don't you admit that the idea is in the highest degree ridiculous?"
10029{_}2054{_}he added more sharply as Gifford remained silent.
10029{_}2055{_}"It is--inconceivable," he admitted abstractedly.
10029{_}2056{_}Kelson, who had taken up his hat and crop and was turning to the door, wheeled round quickly.
10029{_}2057{_}"My dear Hugh," he exclaimed impatiently, "what is the matter with you?
10029{_}2058{_}What monstrous idea have you got in your head?
10029{_}2059{_}You owe it to me, and I really must ask you, to speak out plainly.
10029{_}2060{_}It seems almost an insult to Muriel to ask the question, but do you still persist in the notion that she had, even in the most innocent way, anything to do with Henshaw's death?
10029{_}2061{_}Because I have her positive assurance that she knows nothing of it, beyond what is common knowledge."
10029{_}2062{_}"I too am quite certain of that now," Gifford answered.
10029{_}2063{_}"Why do you say now?"
10029{_}2064{_}Kelson demanded sourly.
10029{_}2065{_}"Surely you never seriously entertained such an abominable idea."
10029{_}2066{_}"You must admit, my dear Harry," Gifford replied calmly, "that with a man stabbed to death in practically the next room, the blood-stains on Miss Tredworth's dress were bound to give rise to conjecture.
10029{_}2067{_}One would suspect an archbishop in a similar position.
10029{_}2068{_}But that is all over now.
10029{_}2069{_}I am as convinced as you can be that Miss Tredworth knew nothing of the business."
10029{_}2070{_}"On your honour that is your opinion?"
10029{_}2071{_}"On my honour."
10029{_}2072{_}"This new discovery has changed your opinion?"
10029{_}2073{_}"It has at least shown me how dangerous it may be to jump to conclusions."
10029{_}2074{_}Kelson drew in a breath.
10029{_}2075{_}"Yes, indeed.
10029{_}2076{_}Poor Muriel has suffered from the suspicion as well as from the horrible shock of the discovery.
10029{_}2077{_}Still, this new development, though it acquits her, does nothing towards solving the mystery.
10029{_}2078{_}I wonder whether Edith Morriston has any idea as to how her dress got marked."
10029{_}2079{_}"I wonder," Gifford responded abstractedly.
10029{_}2080{_}"Well," said Kelson, "I'm off to carry the good news to Muriel.
10029{_}2081{_}Don't wait dinner for me if I'm not back by seven-thirty."
10029{_}2082{_}It was rather a relief to Gifford to be left alone that he might review the situation without interruption.
10029{_}2083{_}His first thought had been, could this last discovery be accountable for what he had seen that afternoon?
10029{_}2084{_}Doubtless, after the information reached the police it would not be long in being conveyed to Henshaw.
10029{_}2085{_}And he was now making use of it to put the screw on, using the hold he had gained over Edith Morriston to bend her to his will.
10029{_}2086{_}What was that?
10029{_}2087{_}Marriage?
10029{_}2088{_}To Gifford the thought was monstrous; yet if it should be that Henshaw had information which put the girl in his power, what could she do?
10029{_}2089{_}That she had consented to meet him secretly and listen to him went to show that she felt her position to be weak.
10029{_}2090{_}If so she might need help, an adviser, a man to stand between her and her persecutor.
10029{_}2091{_}Thinking out the situation strenuously Gifford determined to seek a private interview with Edith Morriston and offer himself as her protector.
10029{_}2092{_}At the worst she could but snub him, and the chances were, he thought, greatly in favour of her accepting his offer of help.
10029{_}2093{_}For from her character he judged she was not a girl to make a stronger appeal to him than the casual invoking of his assistance which had already taken place.
10029{_}2094{_}He had a very cogent reason for believing that he could be of assistance, although there were certain elements in the mystery which might, in his ignorance of them, upset his calculations.
10029{_}2095{_}Anyhow in consideration of the trust Edith Morriston had shown in him he would seek an interview with her and chance what it might bring forth.
10029{_}2096{_}CHAPTER XVI  AN EXPLANATION   In pursuance of this plan Gifford proposed to his friend that they should call at Wynford Place on the next day.
10029{_}2097{_}Kelson had returned from the Tredworths in high spirits, the news he carried there having lifted a weight off his fiancee's mind and indeed restored the happiness of the whole family.
10029{_}2098{_}There was no cloud over the engagement now, and they could all look forward to the marriage without a qualm.
10029{_}2099{_}If Kelson might, in ordinary circumstances, have wondered at the motive for his friend's proposal, which was but thinly disguised, he was in too happy a state of preoccupation to trouble his head about it.
10029{_}2100{_}"I'm your man," he responded promptly.
10029{_}2101{_}"It so happens that Muriel is lunching at Wynford to-morrow, so it will suit me well enough.
10029{_}2102{_}I shouldn't be surprised if we get a note in the morning asking us to lunch there too."
10029{_}2103{_}The morning, however, brought no note of invitation; a failure which rather surprised Kelson, although Gifford thought he could account for it.
10029{_}2104{_}Nevertheless he determined to go and do his best to get a private talk with Edith Morriston, however disinclined she might be to grant it.
10029{_}2105{_}The two men went up to Wynford early in the afternoon, but it was a long time before Gifford got the opportunity he sought.
10029{_}2106{_}Edith Morriston seemed as friendly and gracious as ever, but whether by accident or design she gave no chance for Gifford to get in a private word.
10029{_}2107{_}With the knowledge of what he had seen on the previous afternoon and of the change in her attitude he was too shrewd to show any anxiety for a confidential talk.
10029{_}2108{_}He watched her closely when he could do so unobserved, but her face gave no sign of trouble or embarrassment.
10029{_}2109{_}He wondered if there could after all be anything in his idea of persecution, and the more curious he became the more determined he grew to find out.
10029{_}2110{_}But somehow Miss Morriston contrived that they should never be alone together; when Kelson and Muriel Tredworth strolled off lover-like, Miss Morriston kept her brother with her to make a third.
10029{_}2111{_}The three went round to the stables and inspected the hunters, then through the shrubbery to admire a wonderful bed of snowdrops.
10029{_}2112{_}As they stood there looking over the undulating park, and Gifford, curbing his impatience, was talking of certain changes which had taken place since his early days there, the butler was seen hurrying towards them.
10029{_}2113{_}"Callers, I suppose," Morriston observed with a half-yawn.
10029{_}2114{_}"What is it, Stent?"
10029{_}2115{_}"Could I speak to you, sir?"
10029{_}2116{_}the man said, stopping short a little distance away.
10029{_}2117{_}Morriston went forward to him, and after they had spoken together he turned round, and with an "Excuse me for a few minutes," went off towards the house with the butler.
10029{_}2118{_}So at last the opportunity had come.
10029{_}2119{_}Gifford glanced at his companion and noticed that her face had gone a shade paler than before the interruption.
10029{_}2120{_}"I wonder what can be the matter," she observed, a little anxiously Gifford thought.
10029{_}2121{_}Then she laughed.
10029{_}2122{_}"I dare say it is nothing; Stent is becoming absurdly fussy; and all the alarms and discoveries we have had lately have not diminished the tendency."
10029{_}2123{_}"The latest discovery must have come rather as a relief," Gifford ventured tentatively.
10029{_}2124{_}"The marks on my dress you mean?"
10029{_}2125{_}She laughed.
10029{_}2126{_}"So far that I now share with Muriel Tredworth the suspicion of knowing all about the tragedy."
10029{_}2127{_}"Hardly that," Gifford replied with a smile.
10029{_}2128{_}"There can be no cause for that fear.
10029{_}2129{_}By the way," he added more seriously, "I owe you an account of my failure to gain any information for you with regard to Mr. Gervase Henshaw's plans."
10029{_}2130{_}"He is not communicative?"
10029{_}2131{_}Miss Morriston suggested casually.
10029{_}2132{_}Gifford shook his head.
10029{_}2133{_}"No, I am never able to get hold of him.
10029{_}2134{_}In fact, it seems as though he rather makes a point of avoiding us.
10029{_}2135{_}And if we do meet, he is vagueness and reticence personified."
10029{_}2136{_}They were walking slowly back along the shrubbery path.
10029{_}2137{_}The girl turned to him for an instant, her expression softened in a look of gratitude.
10029{_}2138{_}"It is very kind of you, Mr. Gifford, to take all this trouble for us.
10029{_}2139{_}And I am sure it is not your fault that the result is not what you might wish.
10029{_}2140{_}It was rather absurd of me to set you the task.
10029{_}2141{_}But I am none the less grateful.
10029{_}2142{_}Please think that, and do not bother about it any more."
10029{_}2143{_}"But if the man is likely to annoy you," he urged.
10029{_}2144{_}"Have you longer any reason to fear him?"
10029{_}2145{_}She turned swiftly.
10029{_}2146{_}"Fear him?
10029{_}2147{_}What do you mean?"
10029{_}2148{_}"We thought he might be unscrupulous and might make himself objectionable."
10029{_}2149{_}She shrugged.
10029{_}2150{_}"I dare say it is possible."
10029{_}2151{_}"I must confess," he pursued, "I can't quite make the fellow out.
10029{_}2152{_}Nor his motive for remaining in the place.
10029{_}2153{_}Your brother told me he came across him hanging about in one of your plantations."
10029{_}2154{_}He thought the blood left her face for an instant, but otherwise she showed no sign of discomposure.
10029{_}2155{_}"How did he account for his being there?"
10029{_}2156{_}she asked calmly.
10029{_}2157{_}"Unsatisfactorily enough.
10029{_}2158{_}I forget his actual excuse."
10029{_}2159{_}"Was that all?"
10029{_}2160{_}she demanded coldly.
10029{_}2161{_}"I believe so.
10029{_}2162{_}But it is hardly desirable, as your brother said, to have the man prowling about the property."
10029{_}2163{_}For a moment she was silent.
10029{_}2164{_}"No," she said as though by an afterthought.
10029{_}2165{_}Her manner troubled him.
10029{_}2166{_}"I hope he is not attempting to annoy you," he said searchingly.
10029{_}2167{_}She looked surprised and, he thought, a little resentful at his question.
10029{_}2168{_}"Me?"
10029{_}2169{_}she returned coldly.
10029{_}2170{_}"By hanging about in the plantation?"
10029{_}2171{_}"If he goes no farther than that--"  "Why should he?"
10029{_}2172{_}she demanded in the same rather chilling tone.
10029{_}2173{_}"I don't know," Gifford replied, set back by her manner.
10029{_}2174{_}"Except that I have no high opinion of the fellow.
10029{_}2175{_}It occurred to me he might possibly attempt to persecute you."
10029{_}2176{_}She glanced round at him curiously with a little disdainful smile.
10029{_}2177{_}"What makes you think he would do that?"
10029{_}2178{_}she returned.
10029{_}2179{_}Her attitude was to him not convincing.
10029{_}2180{_}He felt there was a certain reservation beneath the rather cutting tone.
10029{_}2181{_}"I am glad to know there is no question of that," he replied with quiet earnestness.
10029{_}2182{_}"I hope if anything of the kind should occur and you should need a friend you will not overlook me."
10029{_}2183{_}"You are very kind," she responded, but without turning towards him.
10029{_}2184{_}He thought, however, that her low tone had softened, and it gave him hope.
10029{_}2185{_}"I should scarcely take upon myself to suggest this," he said, "but I am emboldened by two facts.
10029{_}2186{_}One that you have already asked me to be your ally, your friend, in this business, the other that there is something about Henshaw and his actions which I do not understand.
10029{_}2187{_}I hope you will forgive my boldness."
10029{_}2188{_}His companion had glanced round now, keenly, as though to probe for the meaning which might lie beneath his words.
10029{_}2189{_}He speculated whether she might be wondering how much he knew; was he cognisant of her meeting with Henshaw?
10029{_}2190{_}But, whatever her thought, she answered in the same even voice, "There is nothing to forgive.
10029{_}2191{_}On the contrary I am most grateful."
10029{_}2192{_}They were nearing the house, and Gifford was debating whether he dared suggest another turn along the shrubbery path, when Richard Morriston appeared at the hall door, beckoned to them, and went in again.
10029{_}2193{_}"I wonder what Dick wants.
10029{_}2194{_}Has anything more come to light?"
10029{_}2195{_}Miss Morriston observed with a rather bored laugh as she slightly quickened her pace.
10029{_}2196{_}As they went in she called, "Dick!"
10029{_}2197{_}and he answered her from the library.
10029{_}2198{_}There they found him with Kelson and Muriel Tredworth.
10029{_}2199{_}A glance at their faces told Gifford that they were all in a state of scarcely suppressed excitement.
10029{_}2200{_}"I say, Edith, what do you think?"
10029{_}2201{_}her brother exclaimed.
10029{_}2202{_}"We've made a rather important discovery.
10029{_}2203{_}Were you in the middle room of the tower during the dance?"
10029{_}2204{_}For a moment his sister did not answer.
10029{_}2205{_}"No; I don't think I was," she said, with what seemed to Gifford a certain amount of apprehension in her eyes, although her expression was calm enough.
10029{_}2206{_}"Oh, but, my dear girl, you must have been," Morriston insisted vehemently.
10029{_}2207{_}"We have found the explanation of the stains on Miss Tredworth's dress and on yours."
10029{_}2208{_}"You have?"
10029{_}2209{_}his sister replied, looking at him curiously.
10029{_}2210{_}"Yes; beyond all doubt.
10029{_}2211{_}The mystery is made clear.
10029{_}2212{_}Come and see."
10029{_}2213{_}He led the way across the hall and up the first story of the tower.
10029{_}2214{_}"There's the explanation," he said, pointing to some dark red patches on the back of a sofa and on the carpet below.
10029{_}2215{_}"It is not a pleasant idea," Morriston said; "but you see these marks are directly under the place where the dead man lay in the room above.
10029{_}2216{_}The blood from his wound evidently ran through the chinks of the flooring on to the beams of the ceiling here and so fell drop by drop on the couch and on any one sitting there.
10029{_}2217{_}Rather gruesome, but I am sure we must be all very glad to get the simple explanation.
10029{_}2218{_}The only wonder is that no one thought of it before."
10029{_}2219{_}"Muriel was sitting just at that end of the sofa when I proposed to her," Kelson said in a low voice to Gifford.
10029{_}2220{_}"I am delighted the matter is so completely accounted for," his friend returned.
10029{_}2221{_}"What fools we were ever to have taken it so tragically."
10029{_}2222{_}But his expression changed as he glanced at Edith Morriston; she had denied that she had been in the room.
10029{_}2223{_}"I have sent down to the police to tell them of the discovery," Morriston was saying.
10029{_}2224{_}"The fact is that since the tragedy the servants appear to have rather shunned this part of the house, or at any rate to have devoted as little time to it as possible.
10029{_}2225{_}Otherwise this would have come to light sooner.
10029{_}2226{_}Anyhow it is a source of congratulation to Miss Tredworth and you, Edith.
10029{_}2227{_}Of course you must have been in here."
10029{_}2228{_}"I remember sitting just there; ugh!"
10029{_}2229{_}Miss Tredworth said with a shudder.
10029{_}2230{_}"I can swear to that," Kelson corroborated with a knowing smile.
10029{_}2231{_}"You must have done the same or brushed against the sofa, Edith," Morriston said cheerfully.
10029{_}2232{_}"Well, I'm glad that's settled, although it brings us no nearer towards solving the mystery of what happened overhead."
10029{_}2233{_}"No," Kelson remarked.
10029{_}2234{_}"It looks as though that was going to remain a mystery."
10029{_}2235{_}The butler came in.
10029{_}2236{_}"Major Freeman is here, sir," he said, "with Mr. Henshaw, and would like to speak to you."
10029{_}2237{_}Morriston looked surprised.
10029{_}2238{_}"Alfred has been very quick.
10029{_}2239{_}We sent him off only about a quarter of an hour ago."
10029{_}2240{_}"Alfred met Major Freeman and Mr. Henshaw with the detective just beyond the lodge gates, sir."
10029{_}2241{_}"Then they were coming up here independently of my message?"
10029{_}2242{_}"Yes, sir.
10029{_}2243{_}Alfred gave Major Freeman the message and came back."
10029{_}2244{_}Morriston moved towards the door.
10029{_}2245{_}"I will see these gentlemen at once," he said.
10029{_}2246{_}"In the library, sir."
10029{_}2247{_}Involuntarily Gifford had glanced at Edith Morriston.
10029{_}2248{_}She was standing impassively with set face; and at his glance she turned away to the window.
10029{_}2249{_}But not before he had caught in her eyes a look which he hated to see, a look which seemed to confirm a suspicion already in his mind.
10029{_}2250{_}CHAPTER XVII  WHAT A GIRL SAW   With Morriston's departure a rather uncomfortable silence fell upon the party left in the room.
10029{_}2251{_}Every one seemed to feel that there was something in the air, the shadow of a possibly serious development in the case.
10029{_}2252{_}Even Kelson, who was otherwise inclined to be jubilant over the freeing of his fiancee from suspicion, seemed to feel it was no time or place just then for gaiety, and his expression grew as grave as that of the rest.
10029{_}2253{_}"I wonder what these fellows have come to say," he observed as he paced the room.
10029{_}2254{_}"Let's hope to announce that at last they are going to leave you in peace, Edith," Miss Tredworth said.
10029{_}2255{_}Edith Morriston did not alter her position as she stood looking out of the window.
10029{_}2256{_}"Thank you for your kind wish, Muriel," she responded in a cold voice; "but I'm afraid that is too much to hope for just yet."
10029{_}2257{_}"Yet one doesn't see what else it can be," Kelson observed reflectively.
10029{_}2258{_}"They can hardly have found out exactly how the man came by his death; much more likely to have abandoned their latest theory, eh, Hugh?"
10029{_}2259{_}Gifford was looking, held by the grip of his imagination, at the tall figure by the window; wondering what was passing behind that veil of impassiveness.
10029{_}2260{_}"I don't see what they can have found out away from this house," he said, rousing himself by an effort to answer; "and they don't seem to have been here lately."
10029{_}2261{_}"Well, we shall see," Kelson said casually.
10029{_}2262{_}"Ah, here comes Dick back again."
10029{_}2263{_}Morriston hurried in with a serious face.
10029{_}2264{_}In answer to Kelson's, "Well, Dick?"
10029{_}2265{_}he said.
10029{_}2266{_}"It appears a rather extraordinary piece of evidence has just come to light; one which, if true, completely solves the mystery of the locked door.
10029{_}2267{_}I asked Freeman if there was any objection to you fellows coming to the library and hearing the story; he is quite agreeable.
10029{_}2268{_}So will you come?
10029{_}2269{_}You too, Edith, and Miss Tredworth; there is nothing at all horrible in it so far."
10029{_}2270{_}For the first time Edith Morriston turned from the window.
10029{_}2271{_}"Is it necessary, Dick?"
10029{_}2272{_}she protested quietly.
10029{_}2273{_}"I'd just as soon hear it all afterwards from you.
10029{_}2274{_}These police visitations are rather getting on my nerves."
10029{_}2275{_}"Very well, dear; you shall hear all about it later on," her brother responded, and led the way down to the library.
10029{_}2276{_}Gifford was the last to leave the room, and his glance back showed him that Edith Morriston had turned again to the window and resumed her former attitude.
10029{_}2277{_}In the library were the chief constable, Gervase Henshaw and a local detective.
10029{_}2278{_}"Now, Major Freeman," Morriston said as he closed the door, "we shall be glad to hear this new piece of evidence."
10029{_}2279{_}Major Freeman bowed.
10029{_}2280{_}"Shortly, it comes to this," he began.
10029{_}2281{_}"A young woman named Martha Haynes, belonging to Branchester, called at my office this morning and made a statement which, if reliable, must have an important bearing on this mysterious case.
10029{_}2282{_}"It appears from her story that on the night of the Hunt Ball held here she had been paying a visit to some friends at Rapscot, a village, as you know, about a mile beyond Wynford.
10029{_}2283{_}On her way back to the town, for which she started at about 9.45, she took as a short cut the right-of-way path running across the park and passing near the house.
10029{_}2284{_}As she went by she was naturally attracted by the lighted windows and could hear the band quite plainly.
10029{_}2285{_}She stopped to listen to the music at a point which she has indicated, almost directly opposite the tower.
10029{_}2286{_}"She says she had stood there for some little time when her attention was suddenly diverted to what seemed a mysterious movement on the outside of the tower.
10029{_}2287{_}A dark body, presumably a human being, appeared to be slowly sliding down the wall from the topmost window.
10029{_}2288{_}Unfortunately before she could quite realize what she was looking at--and we may imagine that a country girl would take some little time to grasp so unusual a situation--a cloud drifted across the moon and threw the tower into shadow.
10029{_}2289{_}"The girl continued, however, to keep her eyes fixed on the spot where she had seen the dark object descending, with the result that in a few seconds she saw it reach and pass over one side of the window of the lower room which was sufficiently lighted up to silhouette anything placed before it.
10029{_}2290{_}She saw the object move slowly over the window and disappear in the darkness beneath it.
10029{_}2291{_}When, a few seconds later, the moon came out again nothing more was to be seen.
10029{_}2292{_}"The girl stayed for some time watching the tower, but without result.
10029{_}2293{_}She is a more or less ignorant, unsophisticated country-woman, and what she had seen she was quite unable to account for.
10029{_}2294{_}Naturally she hardly connected it with any sort of tragical occurrence.
10029{_}2295{_}The house with its lights and music seemed given over to gaiety; that any one should just then have met his death in that upper room never entered her imagination.
10029{_}2296{_}A vague idea that a thief might have got into the house and she had seen him escape by the tower window did indeed, as she says, cross her mind, and that supposition prevented her from approaching the tower to satisfy her curiosity.
10029{_}2297{_}But as nothing more happened she began to think less of the significance of what she had seen, in fact almost persuaded herself that it had been something of an optical delusion.
10029{_}2298{_}Presently, having had enough of standing in the cold wind, she resumed her way, went home and to bed, and early next morning left the town to enter a situation in another part of the country.
10029{_}2299{_}"It appears that she had taken cold by her loitering and soon after reaching her destination became so ill that she had to keep her bed, and it was only on her recovery a few days ago that she heard what had happened here that night.
10029{_}2300{_}Directly she could get away she came over and told her story to us."
10029{_}2301{_}"A pity she could not have come before," Morriston remarked as the chief constable paused.
10029{_}2302{_}"Her evidence is highly important, disposing as it does of the mystery of the locked door."
10029{_}2303{_}"Yes," Major Freeman agreed, "and also of the suicide theory.
10029{_}2304{_}The question now is--who was the person who was seen descending from the window?"
10029{_}2305{_}"Could this girl tell whether it was a man or a woman?"
10029{_}2306{_}The question came from Henshaw, who had hitherto kept silent.
10029{_}2307{_}"She thinks it was a man," Major Freeman answered, "but could not swear to it.
10029{_}2308{_}The fact of the object being close to the wall made it almost impossible in the imperfect light to distinguish plainly.
10029{_}2309{_}But I think we may take it that it was a man.
10029{_}2310{_}The feat could be hardly one a woman would undertake."
10029{_}2311{_}"No," Gifford agreed.
10029{_}2312{_}"And there would seem little chance of identifying the person."
10029{_}2313{_}"None at all so far as the girl Haynes is concerned," Major Freeman replied.
10029{_}2314{_}"But we have something to go upon; a starting point for a new line of inquiry.
10029{_}2315{_}The person seen escaping must have lowered himself by a rope from that top window and a considerable length would be required.
10029{_}2316{_}I have taken the liberty, Mr. Morriston, of setting a party of my men to search the grounds for the rope; they will begin by dragging the little lake."
10029{_}2317{_}"By all means," Morriston assented.
10029{_}2318{_}"Detective Sprules," the chief proceeded, "would like to make another examination of the ironwork of the window.
10029{_}2319{_}May he go up now?"
10029{_}2320{_}"Certainly," Morriston answered, and the detective left the room.
10029{_}2321{_}Gifford spoke.
10029{_}2322{_}"The girl saw nothing of the escaping person after he reached the ground?"
10029{_}2323{_}"Nothing, she says," Major Freeman answered.
10029{_}2324{_}"But the base of the tower was in deep shadow, which would prevent that."
10029{_}2325{_}"A pity her curiosity was not a little more practical," Henshaw observed.
10029{_}2326{_}"Yes."
10029{_}2327{_}Gifford turned to him.
10029{_}2328{_}"You are proved correct, Mr. Henshaw, in your repudiation of the suicide idea.
10029{_}2329{_}Perhaps, in view of this latest development, you may have knowledge to go upon of some one from whom your brother might have apprehended danger?"
10029{_}2330{_}Henshaw's set face gave indication of nothing but a studied reserve.
10029{_}2331{_}"No one certainly," he answered coolly, "from whom he might apprehend danger to his life."
10029{_}2332{_}"There must have been a motive for the act," Kelson observed.
10029{_}2333{_}"Unless it was a sudden quarrel."
10029{_}2334{_}"There appears," Major Freeman put in, "to be no evidence whatever of anything leading up to that."
10029{_}2335{_}"No; the cause is so far quite mysterious," Henshaw said.
10029{_}2336{_}It seemed to Gifford that there was something of undisclosed knowledge behind his words, and he fell to wondering how far the motive was mysterious to him.
10029{_}2337{_}Morriston proceeded to acquaint Major Freeman with the discovered cause of the marks on the ladies' dresses, and they all went off to the lower room where the position of the stains was pointed out.
10029{_}2338{_}Edith Morriston was no longer there.
10029{_}2339{_}"Miss Tredworth sat at this end of the sofa," Morriston explained, "and so the marks on her dress are clearly accounted for."
10029{_}2340{_}"And Miss Morriston?"
10029{_}2341{_}Henshaw put the question in a tone which had in it, Gifford thought, a touch of scepticism.
10029{_}2342{_}"Oh, my sister must have been in here too," Morriston replied.
10029{_}2343{_}"Or how could her dress have been stained?
10029{_}2344{_}Unless, indeed, she brushed against Miss Tredworth's or someone else's.
10029{_}2345{_}That's clear."
10029{_}2346{_}There seemed no alacrity in Henshaw to accept the conclusion and he did not respond.
10029{_}2347{_}"I am glad this part of the mystery is so satisfactorily settled," the chief constable remarked.
10029{_}2348{_}"Now we have the issue narrowed.
10029{_}2349{_}Well, Sprules?"
10029{_}2350{_}The detective had appeared at the door.
10029{_}2351{_}"I have examined the ironwork of the window, sir," he said, "and have found under the magnifying-glass traces of the fraying of a rope as though caused by friction against the iron staple."
10029{_}2352{_}"Sufficient signs to bear out the young woman's statement?"
10029{_}2353{_}"Quite, sir.
10029{_}2354{_}There is upon close examination distinct evidence of a rope having been worked against the hinge of the window."
10029{_}2355{_}"Very good, Sprules.
10029{_}2356{_}We may consider that point settled," Major Freeman said.
10029{_}2357{_}Having finally satisfied themselves as to the cause of the stains on the floor and sofa, the chief constable and his subordinate proposed to go to the lake and see whether the men who were dragging it had had any success.
10029{_}2358{_}Morriston and Henshaw with Kelson and Gifford accompanied them.
10029{_}2359{_}As they came in sight of the boat the detective exclaimed, "They have found it!"
10029{_}2360{_}and the men were seen hauling up a rope out of the water.
10029{_}2361{_}"Sooner than I expected," Major Freeman observed as they hurried towards the nearest point to the boat.
10029{_}2362{_}The rope when landed proved to be of considerable length, sufficient when doubled, they calculated, to reach from the topmost window to within five or six feet of the ground.
10029{_}2363{_}"The escaping person," Henshaw said, "must have slid down the doubled rope which had been passed through the staple of the window, and then when the ground was reached have pulled it away, coiled it up, carried it to the lake, and thrown it in.
10029{_}2364{_}Obviously that was the procedure and it accounts completely for the locked door."
10029{_}2365{_}The chief constable and the detective agreed.
10029{_}2366{_}"A man would want some nerve to come down from that height," the latter remarked.
10029{_}2367{_}"Any man, or woman either for that matter," Henshaw returned dogmatically, "would not hesitate to take the risk as an alternative to being trapped up there with his victim."
10029{_}2368{_}"You are not suggesting it might have been a woman who was seen sliding down the rope?"
10029{_}2369{_}Gifford asked pointedly.
10029{_}2370{_}Henshaw shrugged.
10029{_}2371{_}"I suggest nothing as to the person's identity," he replied in a sharply guarded tone.
10029{_}2372{_}"That is now what remains to be discovered."
10029{_}2373{_}CHAPTER XVIII  THE LOST BROOCH   The police authorities with Henshaw and Morriston went off with the rope to experiment in the room of the tragedy.
10029{_}2374{_}"I don't suppose we are wanted," Kelson said quietly to Gifford; "let's go for a turn round the garden.
10029{_}2375{_}I wonder where Muriel has got to."
10029{_}2376{_}They found Miss Tredworth on the lawn.
10029{_}2377{_}"I am waiting for Edith," she said.
10029{_}2378{_}"We'll stroll on and Gifford can bring Miss Morriston after us," Kelson suggested, and the lovers moved away, leaving Gifford, much to his satisfaction, waiting for Edith Morriston.
10029{_}2379{_}In a few minutes she made her appearance.
10029{_}2380{_}Gifford mentioned the arrangement and they strolled off by the path the others had taken.
10029{_}2381{_}It seemed to Gifford that his companion's manner was rather abnormal; unlike her usual cold reserve there were signs of a certain suppressed excitement.
10029{_}2382{_}"I hope," she said, "that Major Freeman and his people are satisfied with our discovery that the marks on Muriel's dress and mine came there by accident."
10029{_}2383{_}"Evidently quite convinced," Gifford answered.
10029{_}2384{_}"That's well," she responded with a rather forced laugh.
10029{_}2385{_}"It was rather too bad to suspect us, on that evidence, of knowing anything about the affair."
10029{_}2386{_}"I don't suppose for a moment they did," Gifford assured her.
10029{_}2387{_}"I don't know," the girl returned.
10029{_}2388{_}"Anyhow it was rather an embarrassing, not to say painful, position for us to be in.
10029{_}2389{_}But that is at an end now."
10029{_}2390{_}Nevertheless Gifford could tell that she was not so thoroughly relieved as her words implied.
10029{_}2391{_}"Completely," he declared.
10029{_}2392{_}"You have heard of the new piece of evidence?"
10029{_}2393{_}he added casually.
10029{_}2394{_}For a moment she stopped with a start, instantly recovering herself.
10029{_}2395{_}"No; what is that?"
10029{_}2396{_}in a tone almost of unconcern.
10029{_}2397{_}Gifford told her of the statement made by the country girl and its corroboration in the finding of the rope.
10029{_}2398{_}As he continued he felt sure that the story was gripping his companion more and more closely.
10029{_}2399{_}At last she stopped dead and turned to him with eyes which had in them intense mystification as well as fear.
10029{_}2400{_}"Mr. Gifford, do you believe that story?"
10029{_}2401{_}"I see no reason for disbelieving it," he answered quietly.
10029{_}2402{_}"It is practically the only conceivable solution of the mystery of the locked door."
10029{_}2403{_}"Surely--" she stopped, checking the vehement objection that rose to her lips.
10029{_}2404{_}"This girl," she went on as though searching for a plausible argument, "is it not likely that she was mistaken?
10029{_}2405{_}We know what these country people are.
10029{_}2406{_}And she could not have seen very clearly."
10029{_}2407{_}"But," Gifford argued gently, "her statement is confirmed by the finding of the rope."
10029{_}2408{_}Edith Morriston was thinking strenuously, desperately, he could see that.
10029{_}2409{_}The words she spoke were but mechanical, the mere froth of a seething brain.
10029{_}2410{_}Yet her splendid self-command--and he recognized it with admiration--never deserted her, however supreme the struggle may have been to retain it.
10029{_}2411{_}A seat was by them; she went across the path to it and sat down.
10029{_}2412{_}Gifford saw that she was deadly pale.
10029{_}2413{_}"I fear this wretched business is upsetting you, Miss Morriston," he said gently.
10029{_}2414{_}"Let me run to the house and fetch something to revive you."
10029{_}2415{_}She made a gesture to stay him, and by an effort seemed to shake off the threatening collapse.
10029{_}2416{_}"No, no," she said; "please don't.
10029{_}2417{_}It is very stupid of me, but these repeated shocks are rather trying.
10029{_}2418{_}You see one has never had any experience of the sort before."
10029{_}2419{_}"It was more than stupid of me to blunder into the story," Gifford said self-reproachfully.
10029{_}2420{_}"But it never occurred to me--"  "No, no; of course not," she responded.
10029{_}2421{_}"And, after all, I am bound to hear all about it sooner or later.
10029{_}2422{_}Sit down and tell me your opinion of the affair.
10029{_}2423{_}Supposing the girl was not mistaken who do you think the person seen escaping from the window could have been?"
10029{_}2424{_}"That is difficult to say."
10029{_}2425{_}"A thief, no doubt."
10029{_}2426{_}"That is a natural conclusion."
10029{_}2427{_}"Have the police any idea?"
10029{_}2428{_}"Not that I know of.
10029{_}2429{_}I should say decidedly no definite idea."
10029{_}2430{_}"Or Mr.
10029{_}2431{_}Henshaw?"
10029{_}2432{_}"Whatever Mr. Henshaw's ideas may be he keeps them to himself."
10029{_}2433{_}Miss Morriston checked the remark she had seemed about to make, and for a few minutes there was an awkward silence.

10029{_}2436{_}Believe me, it has not been for want of trying.
10029{_}2437{_}But the man, for reasons best known to himself, seems determined to remain inscrutable."
10029{_}2438{_}The girl was staring in front of her.

10029{_}2440{_}But it does not much matter.

10029{_}2442{_}And now please do not think any more of it.
10029{_}2443{_}In my ignorance of the man's character I set you an impossible task.
10029{_}2444{_}All I can do now is to thank you for your sympathy and devotion."
10029{_}2445{_}Her tone pained him horribly.

10029{_}2447{_}She gave a little bitter laugh.
10029{_}2448{_}"Seeing that it is useless I have no right to ask its continuance," she replied almost coldly, "nor to expect you to involve yourself in my--in our worries."
10029{_}2449{_}"But if I ask to be allowed that privilege?"
10029{_}2450{_}he urged.
10029{_}2451{_}She shook her head.

10029{_}2454{_}To involve yourself with him can bring you nothing but trouble.
10029{_}2455{_}Promise me you will take no further heed of this unhappy business."
10029{_}2456{_}She turned to him as she spoke the last words, and there seemed less trouble in her face than in his.
10029{_}2457{_}For at his heart there was a sickening fear and suspicion of what the words portended.
10029{_}2458{_}"I can't promise that," he objected.

10029{_}2461{_}he rejoined.
10029{_}2462{_}"For both.
10029{_}2463{_}Give me your promise.
10029{_}2464{_}You must if we are to remain friends."
10029{_}2465{_}Her look and the fascination in her voice seemed to pull the very heart out of him.
10029{_}2466{_}"You are asking a cruelly hard thing of me," he replied, with a tremor in his voice.
10029{_}2467{_}"I don't understand--"  "No, you don't understand," she interrupted quickly.
10029{_}2468{_}"It is enough to know that you have taken a girl's foolish commission too seriously, so seriously as to run the risk of making things even worse than they threatened to be.
10029{_}2469{_}Now I ask you to leave well alone."
10029{_}2470{_}"If it is well," he said doubtfully.
10029{_}2471{_}"Of course.
10029{_}2472{_}Why should it not be?"
10029{_}2473{_}she rejoined, in a not very convincing tone.
10029{_}2474{_}"Now I shall rely on you--and I am sure it will not be in vain--to respect my wishes.
10029{_}2475{_}Things seem to be in a horrible muddle," she added with a rather dreary laugh, "but let's hope they will right themselves before long."
10029{_}2476{_}She rose, compelling him to rise too.
10029{_}2477{_}Something in the tone and manner of her last speech made him quite unwilling to end their conference, and desperately anxious to speak out everything that was in his mind and try to bring matters to a crisis.
10029{_}2478{_}"Don't go for a moment," he said as she began to move away towards the house.
10029{_}2479{_}"I have something to say to you."
10029{_}2480{_}She turned quickly and faced him with a suggestion of displeasure in her eyes.
10029{_}2481{_}"What is it?"
10029{_}2482{_}she said with a touch of impatience.
10029{_}2483{_}"Only this," he answered quietly.
10029{_}2484{_}"Have you lost a brooch, Miss Morriston?"
10029{_}2485{_}At the question the blood left her cheeks as it had done a little while before; then surged back till her face was suffused.
10029{_}2486{_}"A brooch?
10029{_}2487{_}Yes; I have missed one.
10029{_}2488{_}Have you found it?"
10029{_}2489{_}The words were spoken with a calmness which failed to hide the eagerness behind them.
10029{_}2490{_}"I think so," he answered, taking out his letter-case.

10029{_}2492{_}He opened the case and showed it pinned into the soft lining.
10029{_}2493{_}"Yes; that is mine," she said; and for a moment or two by a strange attraction each looked into the other's eyes.
10029{_}2494{_}Gifford bent his head over the case as he unfastened the brooch and took it out.

10029{_}2496{_}Something in the girl's voice made him glad that he was not looking at her.
10029{_}2497{_}"In the garden," he said.
10029{_}2498{_}"In the garden?"
10029{_}2499{_}she repeated.
10029{_}2500{_}He was looking up now and saw the intense relief in her face.
10029{_}2501{_}"To-day?"
10029{_}2502{_}"No; last time I was up here.
10029{_}2503{_}I ought to have taken it to the house at once but--but it was a temptation to me to keep it till I could give it back to you like this.

10029{_}2505{_}It was plain she divined what he meant, but her cold manner came to the aid of her embarrassment.
10029{_}2506{_}"I am only too glad to have it again.
10029{_}2507{_}I am so glad you found it."
10029{_}2508{_}"So am I," he responded with a touch of fervour.
10029{_}2509{_}"I wish I could relieve your mind of everything else as easily."
10029{_}2510{_}"I am sure you do," she said wistfully, and impulsively half put out her hand.
10029{_}2511{_}He caught it as she was in the act of checking the action and drawing it back.
10029{_}2512{_}"You may be sure--quite sure, of my devotion," he said, and raised her hand to his lips.
10029{_}2513{_}An exclamation and a sudden start as the hand was quickly withdrawn made him look up.
10029{_}2514{_}Edith Morriston's eyes were fixed with something like fear on an object behind him.
10029{_}2515{_}An intuition told him what it was before he looked round to see Henshaw, with his characteristic, rather stealthy walk, coming towards them.
10029{_}2516{_}Gifford set his teeth hard as the two faced round and awaited Henshaw's approach.
10029{_}2517{_}"This man shall not annoy you," he said in an undertone.
10029{_}2518{_}"Don't quarrel with him, for heaven's sake," she entreated in the same tone, under her breath, as the disturbing presence drew near.
10029{_}2519{_}There was a strange excitement in her voice, though none in the set face.
10029{_}2520{_}"I think your brother is looking for you, Miss Morriston," Henshaw said in his even voice when he was within a dozen paces of them.
10029{_}2521{_}"I was just going to look for him," the girl replied in a voice strangely changed from that in which she had talked with Gifford.
10029{_}2522{_}"Isn't it lucky?
10029{_}2523{_}Mr. Gifford has picked up in the garden a brooch I lost some days ago.
10029{_}2524{_}I did not dare to tell Dick, as it was his gift."
10029{_}2525{_}Henshaw gave a casual glance at the ornament.
10029{_}2526{_}"I congratulate you," he responded coolly.
10029{_}2527{_}Then Gifford saw his eyes seek hers as he added: "Where was it found?
10029{_}2528{_}Near the tower?"
10029{_}2529{_}The covert malice of the insinuation was plain in the questioner's look, although the tone was casual enough.
10029{_}2530{_}"No.
10029{_}2531{_}On the lawn," Gifford replied quietly.
10029{_}2532{_}CHAPTER XIX  IN THE CHURCHYARD   Nothing more of importance happened that day at Wynford, and Gifford had no further opportunity of private talk with Edith Morriston.
10029{_}2533{_}But it was evident to him, and the knowledge gave him intense concern, that the girl went in fear of Gervase Henshaw.
10029{_}2534{_}That he was intimidating her, and using his brother's death for that purpose, was beyond doubt, and the very fact that Edith Morriston was a woman of uncommon courage and self-control, one who in ordinary circumstances would be the last to give way to fear or submit to bullying, showed how serious the matter had become.
10029{_}2535{_}Gifford on his part determined that this intolerable state of things must come to an end, and that in spite of the command laid upon him by the girl, he would now pit himself against her persecutor.
10029{_}2536{_}He had given no actual promise, and even if he had it would have been drawn from him in ignorance of certain means which he possessed of help in this crisis.
10029{_}2537{_}And a significant circumstance which came to Gifford's knowledge a day or two after his interview with Edith Morriston in the garden of Wynford, was the cause of his beginning to take action without further delay.
10029{_}2538{_}Late on the next Sunday afternoon Gifford had gone for a country walk which he had arranged to bring him round in time for the evening service at the little village church of Wynford standing just outside the park boundary.
10029{_}2539{_}His way took him by well-remembered field-paths which, although towards the end of his walk darkness had set in, he had no difficulty in tracing.
10029{_}2540{_}The last field he crossed brought him to a by-road joining the highway which ran through Wynford, the junction being about a quarter of a mile from the church.
10029{_}2541{_}As he neared the stile which admitted to the road he saw, on the other side of the hedge and showing just above it, the head of a man.
10029{_}2542{_}At the sound of his footsteps the man quickly turned, and, as for a moment the fitful moonlight caught his face, Gifford was sure he recognized Gervase Henshaw.
10029{_}2543{_}But he took no notice and kept on his way to the stile, which he crossed and gained the road.
10029{_}2544{_}As he did so he glanced back.
10029{_}2545{_}A horse and trap was waiting there with Henshaw in it.
10029{_}2546{_}He was now bending down, probably with the object of concealing his identity, and had moved on a few paces farther down the road.
10029{_}2547{_}Why was he waiting there?
10029{_}2548{_}Gifford asked himself the obvious question with a decidedly uneasy feeling.
10029{_}2549{_}Henshaw the Londoner, on a Sunday evening, waiting with a horse and trap in an unfrequented lane, a road which ran nowhere but to a farm.
10029{_}2550{_}What did it mean?
10029{_}2551{_}Naturally Gifford's suspicions connected Edith Morriston with the circumstance, and yet he told himself the idea was monstrously improbable.
10029{_}2552{_}It was more likely that Henshaw was bound upon some search with the police.
10029{_}2553{_}His movements were and had been for some time mysterious enough.
10029{_}2554{_}Gifford's impulse as he turned into the high road was to stay there in concealment and watch for the upshot of Henshaw's presence.
10029{_}2555{_}The suggestion did not, however, altogether commend itself to him.
10029{_}2556{_}He disliked the idea of spying even upon such a man as Henshaw, whom he had good reason to suspect of playing a dastardly game.
10029{_}2557{_}It was probable, too, that Henshaw had recognized him and might be on the look-out; it would be intensely humiliating to be caught watching.
10029{_}2558{_}So, turning the pros and cons over in his mind, Gifford walked slowly on in a state of irresolution till he came to a wicket-gate which admitted from the road to a path which ran through the churchyard.
10029{_}2559{_}There he stopped, debating with himself whether he should turn back and keep an eye on Henshaw or go on into the church where service was just beginning.
10029{_}2560{_}It did seem absurd to imagine that Henshaw with his conveyance could be waiting there by appointment for a girl of the character and position of Edith Morriston.
10029{_}2561{_}True, he had seen them walking together in secret, which was strange enough, but that need not necessarily have been a planned meeting.
10029{_}2562{_}Such an urgent curiosity had hold of him at the bare possibility of something wrong that he, temporizing with his scruples, was about to turn back to the lane, when he saw the figure of a woman coming towards him along the churchyard path.
10029{_}2563{_}She was tall and so far as he could make out, muffled in a cloak and veil.
10029{_}2564{_}His heart gave a leap, for although the woman's face and figure were indistinguishable the height and gait corresponded with those of Edith Morriston.
10029{_}2565{_}As she came near the little gate where he stood she stopped dead, seemed to hesitate a moment, and then turned as though to go back.
10029{_}2566{_}Determined to set his doubts at rest Gifford passed quickly through the gate and followed her at an overtaking pace.
10029{_}2567{_}Evidently sensible of her pursuit, the woman quickened her steps and, as Gifford gained on her, turned quickly from the path, threading her way among the graves to escape him.
10029{_}2568{_}She had gone but a few steps when in her hurry she tripped over the mound of a small, unmarked grave and fell to the ground.
10029{_}2569{_}Gifford ran to her and taking her arm assisted her to rise.
10029{_}2570{_}"Miss Morriston!"
10029{_}2571{_}he exclaimed, for he now was sure of her identity.
10029{_}2572{_}"I hope you are not hurt," he added mechanically, his mind full of a greater and more critical contingency.
10029{_}2573{_}"Mr.
10029{_}2574{_}Gifford!"
10029{_}2575{_}she responded; but he was sure she had not recognized him then for the first time.
10029{_}2576{_}"Oh, no, thank you; I am not in the least hurt.
10029{_}2577{_}It was stupid of me to trip and fall like that.
10029{_}2578{_}Are you going to church?"
10029{_}2579{_}she added, evidently wishing to get away.
10029{_}2580{_}"I was," he answered.
10029{_}2581{_}"And you?"
10029{_}2582{_}"I was too," she said, conquering her embarrassment, "but I have a headache, and prefer the fresh air.
10029{_}2583{_}Don't let me keep you," she held out her hand.
10029{_}2584{_}"Service has begun."
10029{_}2585{_}He took her hand.
10029{_}2586{_}"Miss Morriston," he said gravely, "don't think me very unmannerly, but I am not going to leave you here."
10029{_}2587{_}In the bright moonlight he could see her expression of rather haughty surprise.

10029{_}2591{_}"Is he?"
10029{_}2592{_}The same defiant note; but there was anxiety behind the cold pretence.
10029{_}2593{_}"Yes.
10029{_}2594{_}And pardon me, I have an idea he is waiting there for you."

10029{_}2598{_}But her lip trembled and her voice was scarcely steady.
10029{_}2599{_}"It is something to me," he replied insistently, "because it means a great deal to you.
10029{_}2600{_}This man is persecuting you.
10029{_}2601{_}He is--"  "Mr.
10029{_}2602{_}Gifford!"
10029{_}2603{_}she exclaimed.
10029{_}2604{_}"You take--"  He held up his hand.

10029{_}2606{_}I can convince you that I am not taking too much upon myself.
10029{_}2607{_}I am no fool and am not interfering without warrant.

10029{_}2609{_}That is very far from being the case, and I can prove it."
10029{_}2610{_}"I don't understand you, Mr.
10029{_}2611{_}Gifford."
10029{_}2612{_}The tone of cold annoyance was gone now.
10029{_}2613{_}Relief and a vague hope seemed to be struggling with an almost overwhelming anxiety.
10029{_}2614{_}"You will understand directly," he replied.
10029{_}2615{_}"I have more than a suspicion that this man is seeking to connect you with his brother's death and is making use of a certain half-knowledge he possesses to get a hold over you.
10029{_}2616{_}Is that not so?"
10029{_}2617{_}For a while she was silent, her breath coming quickly, as she hesitated how to meet the direct question.

10029{_}2619{_}At length she spoke.
10029{_}2620{_}"Mr. Gifford, I trust you as a man of honour.
10029{_}2621{_}Your conjecture is right, but unhappily there is no help for it."
10029{_}2622{_}"There is help," he declared reassuringly.

10029{_}2624{_}The girl gave a shiver.

10029{_}2629{_}"And with that idea he terrorizes you?"
10029{_}2630{_}The question was put with quiet sternness.
10029{_}2631{_}"Yes, yes; but I cannot help it!
10029{_}2632{_}I cannot bear it.
10029{_}2633{_}Oh, let me go."
10029{_}2634{_}She seemed now in an agony of fear.
10029{_}2635{_}Gifford laid his hand on her as she sought to move away towards the gate and the waiting enemy.
